	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">International Phonetic Alphabet</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable"><div style="display:inline;" class="plainlinks selfreference noprint">For an introductory guide on IPA symbols with audio, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>. For the usage of the IPA on Wikipedia, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Introduction" title="Help:IPA/Introduction">Help:IPA/Introduction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">Help:IPA/English</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Conventions_for_English" title="Help:IPA/Conventions for English">Help:IPA/Conventions for English</a>.</div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the ICAO spelling alphabet, see <a href="/wiki/ICAO_spelling_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="ICAO spelling alphabet">ICAO spelling alphabet</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO_spelling_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO spelling alphabet">NATO spelling alphabet</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Alphabetic system of phonetic notation</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;padding:0.25em; background:white; color:black;;">International Phonetic Alphabet<br /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047488">.mw-parser-output .nobold{font-weight:normal}</style><span class="nobold"></span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding-top:0.4em;padding-bottom:0.4em;"><a href="/wiki/File:IPA_in_IPA.svg" class="image"><img alt="IPA in IPA.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/IPA_in_IPA.svg/200px-IPA_in_IPA.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="53" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/IPA_in_IPA.svg/300px-IPA_in_IPA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/IPA_in_IPA.svg/400px-IPA_in_IPA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="562" data-file-height="148" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Type</th><td><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;line-height:1.25em">     Alphabet, partially <a href="/wiki/Featural_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Featural alphabet">featural</a>
          </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Languages</th><td>Used for <a href="/wiki/Phonetics" title="Phonetics">phonetic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemic</a> transcription of any language</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Time period</div></th><td>since 1888</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Parent systems</div></th><td><div style="padding-top:0.15em;"><a href="/wiki/Palaeotype_alphabet" title="Palaeotype alphabet">Palaeotype alphabet</a><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Romic_alphabet" title="Romic alphabet">Romic alphabet</a><ul style="margin-left:0.8em;"><li><a href="/wiki/Phonotypic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Phonotypic alphabet">Phonotypic alphabet</a><ul style="margin-left:0.8em;"><li>International Phonetic Alphabet</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Direction</th><td>Left-to-right</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><a href="/wiki/ISO_15924" title="ISO 15924">ISO 15924</a></th><td><code>Latn, 215</code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Unicode alias</div></th><td>Latin</td></tr></tbody></table>
<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width:1px"></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Phonetics" title="Phonetics">phonetic</a> <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbols</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>&#32;instead of phonetic symbols.</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The <b>International Phonetic Alphabet</b> (<b>IPA</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">alphabetic</a> system of <a href="/wiki/Phonetic_transcription" title="Phonetic transcription">phonetic notation</a> based primarily on the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>. It was devised by the <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Association" title="International Phonetic Association">International Phonetic Association</a> in the late <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th century</a> as a standardized representation of the sounds of <a href="/wiki/Spoken_language" title="Spoken language">spoken language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IPA_1999_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPA_1999-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The IPA is used by <a href="/wiki/Lexicography" title="Lexicography">lexicographers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_language" title="Foreign language">foreign language</a> students and teachers, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speech-language_pathology" title="Speech-language pathology">speech-language pathologists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">singers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">actors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constructed_language" title="Constructed language">constructed language</a> creators and <a href="/wiki/Translation" title="Translation">translators</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-world_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The IPA is designed to represent only those qualities of speech that are part of oral language: <a href="/wiki/Phone_(phonetics)" title="Phone (phonetics)">phones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intonation_(linguistics)" title="Intonation (linguistics)">intonation</a> and the separation of <a href="/wiki/Word" title="Word">words</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllables</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IPA_1999_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPA_1999-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> To represent additional qualities of speech, such as tooth gnashing, <a href="/wiki/Lisp" title="Lisp">lisping</a>, and sounds made with a <a href="/wiki/Cleft_lip_and_cleft_palate" title="Cleft lip and cleft palate">cleft lip and cleft palate</a>, an extended set of symbols, the <a href="/wiki/Extensions_to_the_International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Extensions to the International Phonetic Alphabet">extensions to the International Phonetic Alphabet</a>, may be used.<sup id="cite_ref-world_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IPA symbols are composed of one or more elements of two basic types, <a href="/wiki/Letter_(alphabet)" title="Letter (alphabet)">letters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>. For example, the sound of the English letter &#x27e8;t&#x27e9; may be transcribed in IPA with a single letter, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t]</span>, or with a letter plus diacritics, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t̺ʰ]</span>, depending on how precise one wishes to be.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> Often, slashes are used to signal <a href="/wiki/Phonetic_transcription#Narrow_versus_broad_transcription" title="Phonetic transcription">broad or phonemic transcription</a>; thus, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t/</span> is less specific than, and could refer to, either <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t̺ʰ]</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t]</span>, depending on the context and language.
</p><p>Occasionally letters or diacritics are added, removed or modified by the International Phonetic Association. As of the most recent change in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> there are 107 letters, 52 diacritics and four <a href="/wiki/Prosody_(linguistics)" title="Prosody (linguistics)">prosodic</a> marks in the IPA. These are shown in the current <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet_chart" title="International Phonetic Alphabet chart">IPA chart</a>, also posted below in this article and at the website of the IPA.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
